In the Pa├▒caviс╣Г┼Ыa Br─Бhmaс╣Зa<sup>9</sup> the <b>Vr─Бtyas,</b> Hindus without the pale of Brahminism, are described as not cultivating the soil. <dvsn n='P'/>The plough land was called <b>Urvar─Б</b> or <b>Kс╣гetra;</b> manure (<b>┼Ъakan, Kar─лс╣гa</b>) was used, and irrigation was practised (<b>Khani-</b> <b>tra</b>). The plough (<b>L─Бс╣Еgala, S─лra</b>) was drawn by oxen, teams of six, eight, or even twelve being employed.<sup>10</sup> The operations of agriculture are neatly summed up in the ┼Ъatapatha Br─Бhmaс╣Зa<sup>11</sup> as тАШploughing, sowing, reaping, and threshingтАЩ (<i>kс╣Ыс╣гantaс╕е,</i> <i>vapantaс╕е, lunantaс╕е, mс╣Ыс╣Зantaс╕е</i>). The ripe grain was cut with a sickle (<b>D─Бtra, Sс╣Ыс╣Зi</b>), bound into bundles<sup>12</sup> (<b>Parс╣гa</b>), and beaten out on the floor of the granary (<b>Khala</b>).<sup>13</sup> The grain was then separated from the straw and refuse either by a sieve (<b>Titau</b>) or a winnowing fan (<b>┼Ъ┼лrpa</b>).<sup>14</sup> The winnower was called <b>Dh─Бny─Бkс╣Ыt,</b><sup>15</sup> and the grain was measured in a vessel called <b>Urdara.</b><sup>16</sup> <dvsn n='P'/>The Rigveda leaves us in doubt as to the kind of grain grown, for <b>Yava</b> is a word of doubtful signification, and <b>Dh─Бn─Б</b> is also vague. In the later Saс╣Гhit─Бs<sup>17</sup> things are different. Rice (<b>Vr─лhi</b>) appears, Yava means barley, with a species styled <b>Upav─Бka.</b> Beans (<b>Mudga, M─Бс╣гa</b>), sesamum (<b>Tila</b>), and other grains (<b>Aс╣Зu, Khalva, Godh┼лma, N─лv─Бra, Priyaс╣Еgu,</b> <b>Mas┼лra, ┼Ъy─Бm─Бka</b>) are mentioned, while cucumbers (<b>Urv─Бr┼л,</b> <b>Ury─Бr┼лka</b>) were known. It is uncertain whether fruit trees (<b>Vс╣Ыkс╣гa</b>) were cultivated, or merely grew wild;<sup>18</sup> but frequent mention is made of the jujube (<b>Karkandhu, Kuvala, Badara.</b>). <dvsn n='P'/>The seasons for agriculture are briefly summed up in a passage of the Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б:<sup>19</sup> barley ripened in summer, being no doubt sown, as in modern India, in winter; rice ripened in autumn, being sown in the beginning of the rains; beans and sesamum, planted at the time of the summer rains, ripened in the winter and the cool season. There were two harvests (<b>Sasya</b>) a year according to the Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б;<sup>20</sup> the winter crop was ripe by the month of Caitra (March-April) according to the Kauс╣г─лtaki Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.<sup>21</sup> <dvsn n='P'/>The farmer had plenty of trouble of his own: moles destroyed the seed, birds and various kinds of reptiles (<b>Upakvasa, Jabhya,</b> <b>Tarda, Pataс╣Еga</b>) injured the young shoots, excessive rain or drought might damage the crops.
